### Post by poofyhairguy on 2005-05-09
One thing that I noticed Ubuntu really needed was a place for newer users to be able to find out what apps to use. I know when I first started Linux less than a year ago, my biggest questions were "where is the Linux winamp" or "what is the Linux version of _______ program." So the purpose of this thread it to make a conversion chart. This will be a work in progress for a long time, so please chime in with good ideas for conversions.  Only open source stuff please, and only the most developed programs in each category so as to not confuse. And nothing that isn't in the main/universe also please. I will also list programs that have Window's or OSX ports since a new user might not have any experiance with OSS).

Windows to Linux Conversion:

In Windows                   ---------                                                          In Ubuntu

Internet Explorer               ---------                                                    Firefox

Microsoft Office                           ---------                                             OpenOffice.org

Winamp                   --------                                                                 Xmms

Photoshop                   ---------                                                             Gimp

AIM, ICQ, MSN, Yahoo!, Jabber, IRC  instant messaging                 ---------                                          Gaim
  
Word Pad (or notepad)                  ---------                                            Gedit

Windows Media Player                        ---------                                       Totem

iTunes                          ---------                                                              -for playing music:
                                                                                    -----------------------------Rhythmbox
                                    ----------------------for iPod Syncing
                                                                               --------------------------------Gtkpod

ID3 tag editor ----------------------- easytag




MIRC                               --------                                                             Xchat

Premiere (Movie Editing)              ---------                                              kino

Bittorado                                     ---------                                              Bittorado
                                                                                                  (don't you love  
                                                                                                   native ports)

Dreamweaver                            ---------                                                 Nvu

CDex                               ----------                                                           Sound Juicer 

Nero                                     --------                                                      Gnomebaker

Outlook Express                   ---------                                    Evolution, Thunderbird

Snood                                     ----------                                                   Frozen-bubble

Partition Magic --------- Gparted

eMule ----------- aMule
Soulseek ------------- Nicotine
DC++ -------------- Valknut
any multitorrent client ------------ Azureus
any download manager --------------- D4X or Gwget
regedit -------------------- gconf 

Adobe Illustrator ------------ Inkscape

Remote Desktop Connection ------------ Terminal Server Client

Windows Explorer ------------- Nautilus

Windows Picture and Fax Viewer ------------ Image Viewer (Eye of GNOME)

Paint ------------- Jdraw

Kubuntu:

Internet Explorer --------- Konqueror

Microsoft Office --------- OpenOffice.org/KOffice

Winamp -------- Amarok (with the small view)

Photoshop --------- Gimp

Aol Instant Messenger --------- Kopete

Word Pad (or notepad) --------- Kwrite

Windows Media Player --------- Kaffeine

iTunes --------- -for playing music:
-----------------------------Amarok
-----------------------------Juk
----------------------for iPod Syncing
--------------------------------Gtkpod

MIRC -------- Xchat

Premiere (Movie Editing) --------- kino

Bittorado --------- Azureus QT/Qtorrent
(don't you love
native ports)

Dreamweaver --------- Nvu

CDex ---------- Kaudiocreator

Nero -------- K3B

Outlook Express --------- KMail

Snood ---------- Frozen-bubble

Partition Magic --------- Qparted

EDIT: Here is a much bigger list on another site for those that don't see what they need here:

[http://www.linuxrsp.ru/win-lin-soft/table-eng.html](http://www.linuxrsp.ru/win-lin-soft/table-eng.html)

### Post by TravisNewman on 2005-05-13
murphy2005-- there's a program called gaim, that will let you use your AIM, ICQ, MSN, Yahoo!, Jabber, IRC, and many other accounts through it, and best of all it's more lightweight than any of the windows standalone clients. The only trouble I've had is file transfer. They always seem to work incredibly well over MSN, but I can't get them to work on anything else.

### Post by Jenda on 2005-05-16

---

### Post by Nu-Buntu on 2005-05-16
[QUOTE=Jenda]Why is Evolution better than Thunderbird? (and BTW, that's what it is, not Firebird anymore...)[/QUOTE]

Thunderbird was never Firebird. Firefox was Firebird.

Another, older Open Source database project was also called Firebird, so Mozilla switched it to Firefox to prevent confusion.

---

### Post by Jenda on 2005-05-17

### Post by Terracotta on 2005-05-17

Another, older Open Source database project was also called Firebird, so Mozilla switched it to Firefox to prevent confusion.[/QUOTE]

It is thunderbird that used to be firebird, they changed the name because the name was to confusing with firefox. It was not firefox that used to be firebird, but thunderbird.

### Post by concept10 on 2005-05-18
[QUOTE=Jenda]Why is Evolution better than Thunderbird? (and BTW, that's what it is, not Firebird anymore...)[/QUOTE]

Evolution is more of a full featured email and calendaring application like Outlook.  Its not better than Thunderbird if your're talking about email features.   Thunderbird compares to Outlook Express which it is definitely better than.

---

### Post by zenlord on 2005-05-18
[QUOTE=Terracotta]It is thunderbird that used to be firebird, they changed the name because the name was to confusing with firefox. It was not firefox that used to be firebird, but thunderbird.[/QUOTE]
I don't think so. Nu-buntu was right! Who are you trying to confuse :p?

All mozilla apps started out as -birds (firebird, thunderbird and sunbird), but the firebird-name was already taken by another OS-app, so Mozilla.org decided to change names and artwork for their browser.

Zl. (new to linux, but certainly not new to firebird /-fox ;))

### Post by dustigroove on 2005-05-18
RE: Firefox/Thunderbird naming

[I]Phoenix -> Firebird -> Firefox
Minotaur - > Thunderbird[/I]

See:
[http://www.mozilla.org/projects/firefox/firefox-name-faq.html](http://www.mozilla.org/projects/firefox/firefox-name-faq.html) 
[http://www.mozilla.org/status/2003-04-18.html](http://www.mozilla.org/status/2003-04-18.html)

.

### Post by poofyhairguy on 2005-05-21
[QUOTE=David Kaisemann]Hello there... Any body home? I'm repeat my question: how about analogue of Adobe InDesign for Ubuntu?

Sorry for obtrusiveness.[/QUOTE]

NVU and Bluefish are the big web design tools. 

I think that NVU is the only mature "what you see if what you get" software for Ubuntu. So I could have said:

Adobe InDesign-------NVU

instead of dreamweaver. I picked dreamweaver because it is more popular. If you are asking if there is a project that is trying to copy InDesign, then no I don't think there is.

Try NVU. If you don't like...well.....that might be that.

### Post by ow50 on 2005-05-27
[QUOTE=kes]hello, I was wondering if someone could recommend me analogues for the following Microsoft applications:
- Matematica[/QUOTE]
If you mean Mathematica:
It does run on Linux, but a free replacement would be Maxima. I'd recommend [wxMaxima](http://wxmaxima.sourceforge.net/) as a GUI for that.

The above mentioned Octave would rather be a free replacement for Matlab.

### Post by uc50_ic4more on 2005-05-31
[QUOTE=David Kaisemann]Hello there... Any body home? I'm repeat my question: how about analogue of Adobe InDesign for Ubuntu?

Sorry for obtrusiveness.[/QUOTE]

Scribus.

Finding a suitable replacement for Indy was a primary concern for me before I switched to Linux, and I have been very happy with Scribus.

*If* I recall correctly (and that is never a given...) you may require access to the "Universe" repository to get it.

Also, be mindful that Scribus *cannot* open what .indd files you already have. The only solution I am aware of is to tediously export every .indd document you have as .eps.

I also use Scribus to export CMYK .pdf from RGB files edited in the GIMP. It's an extra step or two, but in the abcense of true CMYK capability in the GIMP...

Good luck!

---

### Post by Xanthous on 2005-06-04
Is Scribus the only "larger" layout appz for linux?  I've worked a lot with **CorelDraw**, and am looking for something with that kind of capabilities.
Thank you!

---

### Post by uc50_ic4more on 2005-06-04
[QUOTE=Xanthous]Is Scribus the only "larger" layout appz for linux?  I've worked a lot with **CorelDraw**, and am looking for something with that kind of capabilities.
Thank you![/QUOTE]

Xanthous -

This depends almost entirely on what you consider "capabilities"... For page layout, pre-press, text layout, etc., Scribus is much more capable than (at least the last version I ever played with...) Corel Draw. On the other hand, for vector ilustration - Draw's stated purpose, Scribus may be left wanting for capability.

There must be somewhere that you can view some screenshots of Scribus to get a sense of what tools are available, no?

---

### Post by twiggy2206 on 2005-06-06
[QUOTE=poofyhairguy]One thing that I noticed Ubuntu really needed was a place for newer users to be able to find out what apps to use. I know when I first started Linux less than a year ago, my biggest questions were "where is the Linux winamp" or "what is the Linux version of _______ program." So the purpose of this thread it to make a conversion chart. This will be a work in progress for a long time, so please chime in with good ideas for conversions.  Only open source stuff please, and only the most developed programs in each category so as to not confuse. And nothing that isn't in the main/universe also please. I will also list programs that have Window's or OSX ports since a new user might not have any experiance with OSS).

Windows to Linux Conversion:

In Windows                   ---------                                                          In Ubuntu

Internet Explorer               ---------                                                    Firefox

Microsoft Office                           ---------                                             OpenOffice.org

Winamp                   --------                                                                 Xmms

Photoshop                   ---------                                                             Gimp

AIM, ICQ, MSN, Yahoo!, Jabber, IRC  instant messaging                 ---------                                          Gaim
  
Word Pad (or notepad)                  ---------                                            Gedit

Windows Media Player                        ---------                                       Totem

Snood                                     ----------                                                   Frozen-bubble

eMule ----------- aMule

### Post by Ampersand on 2005-07-12
[QUOTE=filemanager][http://www.livejournal.com/download/index.bml?platform=X+Window+System](http://www.livejournal.com/download/index.bml?platform=X+Window+System)

Which of those should I use? Drivel? Ubuntu is a Gnome environment right?

If it is Drivel, how would I install it? There doesn't seem to be any documentation on the website. Would it run on amd64?

Just in general, can you install i386 programs on amd64? or do the programs have to be amd64 specific?[/QUOTE]

Drivel is available in the synaptic package manager. I'm currently using it, and it also works with xmms/beep-media-player for the 'currently playing' field.

Anything that you install through synaptic (or apt-get) will run on an amd-64.
-
Richard

### Post by AntiDragon on 2005-07-12
[QUOTE=filemanager]What would be the Linux equivalent to PowerDVD?[/QUOTE]

Totem is provided in a standard install. It's a general purpose media player.
You will need to follow [these instructions](http://www.ubuntuguide.org/#dvdplayback) to enable DVD playback.

For legal (licensing and costs?) reasons, some formats (DVD, MP3) are not playable out of the box.

There are other media players available too.

---

### Post by filemanager on 2005-07-12

is only available from another source

### Post by AntiDragon on 2005-07-12
Heh...I'm running AMD64 as well and there IS a way (I was kinda chuffed when I figured it out)...bare with me, it's from memory...

What I had to do was ensure libdvdread3 was installed (use Synaptic).

You then need to locate a Debian AMD64 package (.deb) for "fakeroot". Can't remember where - I googled for it.

Install it using
```
dpkg -i -force <package name>
```

You can dow run the script provided by libDVDRead3:
```
sudo /usr/share/doc/libdvdread3/examples/install-css.sh
```

This will compile from source (So it's good for AMD64), create a .deb package and install it.

If all goes well (Test it!), you can then un-install Fakeroot. Actually, you could probably leave it but I didn't as I'm uncomfortable with broken packages on my system.. :grin:

---

### Post by filemanager on 2005-07-12
[QUOTE=AntiDragon]Heh...I'm running AMD64 as well and there IS a way (I was kinda chuffed when I figured it out)...bare with me, it's from memory...

What I had to do was ensure libdvdread3 was installed (use Synaptic).

You then need to locate a Debian AMD64 package (.deb) for "fakeroot". Can't remember where - I googled for it.

Install it using
```
dpkg -i -force <package name>
```

You can dow run the script provided by libDVDRead3:
```
sudo /usr/share/doc/libdvdread3/examples/install-css.sh
```

This will compile from source (So it's good for AMD64), create a .deb package and install it.

If all goes well (Test it!), you can then un-install Fakeroot. Actually, you could probably leave it but I didn't as I'm uncomfortable with broken packages on my system.. :grin:[/QUOTE]
 I found fakeroot in Synaptic, installed it from there, then ran the script and I got:

No binary deb available.  Will try to build and install it.
You need to have debhelper, dpkg-dev and fakeroot installed.
If not, interrupt now, install them and rerun this script.

This is higly experimental, look out for what happens below.
If you want to stop, interrupt now (control-c), else press
return to proceed

### Post by filemanager on 2005-07-12
Actually just an update, I found an "updated" (I think) fakeroot package here:

[http://packages.debian.org/cgi-bin/download.pl?arch=amd64&file=pool%2Fmain%2Ff%2Ffakeroot%2Ffakeroot_1.2.10_amd64.deb&md5sum=51775c1c5c976d685809f2c05bbdc249&arch=amd64&type=main](http://packages.debian.org/cgi-bin/download.pl?arch=amd64&file=pool%2Fmain%2Ff%2Ffakeroot%2Ffakeroot_1.2.10_amd64.deb&md5sum=51775c1c5c976d685809f2c05bbdc249&arch=amd64&type=main)

Which I installed using:

sudo dpkg -i --force-depends fakeroot*


I still get the error in my last post though

EDIT: Now when I put a DVD in I get this error message:
"Device "/dev/dsp" does not exist

### Post by AntiDragon on 2005-07-13
For FIlemanager:

Have you searched Synaptic for debhelper and dpkg-dev? You'll need those as part of the script creates a .deb package before installing. Also look for "build-essentials" as this makes sure you have all the compiling tools you need.  Once installed, try the script again. :grin: 

By the way, if you found a fakeroot that worked, stick with that one. The only reason I forced an install was because I coouldn't find fakeroot in the repositories. Use force installs as sparingly as possible - using
[FONT=Courier New]sudo apt-get -f install[/FONT]
will remove all such broken packages from your system.

By the way, would a mod mind moving these last few posts to a new thread? Since we're straying from the topic and all....   :wink:

---

### Post by dshadywun on 2005-07-18
[QUOTE=poofyhairguy]One thing that I noticed Ubuntu really needed was a place for newer users to be able to find out what apps to use. I know when I first started Linux less than a year ago, my biggest questions were "where is the Linux winamp" or "what is the Linux version of _______ program." So the purpose of this thread it to make a conversion chart. This will be a work in progress for a long time, so please chime in with good ideas for conversions.  Only open source stuff please, and only the most developed programs in each category so as to not confuse. And nothing that isn't in the main/universe also please. I will also list programs that have Window's or OSX ports since a new user might not have any experiance with OSS).

Windows to Linux Conversion:

In Windows                   ---------                                                          In Ubuntu

Internet Explorer               ---------                                                    Firefox

Microsoft Office                           ---------                                             OpenOffice.org

Winamp                   --------                                                                 Xmms

Photoshop                   ---------                                                             Gimp

AIM, ICQ, MSN, Yahoo!, Jabber, IRC  instant messaging                 ---------                                          Gaim
  
Word Pad (or notepad)                  ---------                                            Gedit

Windows Media Player                        ---------                                       Totem

iTunes                          ---------                                                              -for playing music:
                                                                                    -----------------------------Rhythmbox
                                    ----------------------for iPod Syncing
                                                                               --------------------------------Gtkpod

ID3 tag editor ----------------------- easytag




MIRC                               --------                                                             Xchat

Bittorado                                     ---------                                              Bittorado
                                                                                                  (don't you love  
                                                                                                   native ports)

Dreamweaver                            ---------                                                 Nvu

CDex                               ----------                                                           Sound Juicer 

Nero                                     --------                                                      Gnomebaker

Outlook Express                   ---------                                    Evolution, Thunderbird

Snood                                     ----------                                                   Frozen-bubble

Partition Magic --------- Gparted

eMule ----------- aMule
Soulseek ------------- Nicotine
DC++ -------------- Valknut
any multitorrent client ------------ Azureus
any download manager --------------- D4X or Gwget
regedit -------------------- gconf 

Adobe Illustrator ------------ Inkscape

Remote Desktop Connection ------------ Terminal Server Client

Windows Explorer ------------- Nautilus

Windows Picture and Fax Viewer ------------ Image Viewer (Eye of GNOME)

Paint ------------- Jdraw

Kubuntu:

Internet Explorer --------- Konqueror

Microsoft Office --------- OpenOffice.org/KOffice

Winamp -------- Amarok (with the small view)

Photoshop --------- Gimp

Aol Instant Messenger --------- Kopete

Word Pad (or notepad) --------- Kwrite

-----------------------------Amarok

----------------------for iPod Syncing

### Post by Strangerdave on 2005-07-30
Just wondering if there was a program that comes with ubuntu that zips and unzips files other than Archive Manager?  I have a file that ends boozers.r01 and I can't open it.

-TS-

---

### Post by Trojan1313 on 2005-07-30
[QUOTE=Strangerdave]Just wondering if there was a program that comes with ubuntu that zips and unzips files other than Archive Manager?  I have a file that ends boozers.r01 and I can't open it.

-TS-[/QUOTE]
With the provided information I'm guessing you don't know this.
.r01 is part one of a series of files, you need all files (how many is undetermined, but it starts with r00 or r01). When you have all these files you open them with your package manager and it should build them together. This system comes from when files were begining to spread on the news servers, and the news server protocol couldn't handle bigger filer than a couple of megabytes or something.

Not 100% on the history, but I think my memory served me right. :)

I don't know if Archive Manager can do this, but I figured it'd be good for you to know that anyway. :)

---

### Post by Strangerdave on 2005-07-30

-SD-

-SD-[/QUOTE]

### Post by MaX on 2005-09-13
[QUOTE=Napasik]How do I start an .EXE file ?
As I understood it .EXE files wont work the same as in Windows.[/QUOTE]
That depends.

Is the .exe file a Mono (C# Compiled) file or is it a windows file?

In the first case ```
mono myfile.exe
or
./myfile.exe
```would work.
In the later```
wine myfile.exe
```

Good luck

### Post by dictator88 on 2005-10-14
Not sure if this is the right place to really post this but in  my frustration I MUST express my plite!  Started computing with Texas insturments and commadore vic's, now own a computer store and build new PC's and repair old ones. This include's tearing about windows and windows software and fixing it. So,,, I would like to think I'm not a dumb ass here. For a year I have off and on jumped into the liunx and unix world. Personally, I believe it is the future if the linux/unix people start talking (human) to humans to explain the linux/unix world. That being said, here is my issue. 
Finding ubuntu is a mixed blessing. Easy install, basics are already there, (web,mail), but for the love GOD going beyound that point isn't just a "Learning curve", if a leap of faith into the abyss of jipper jabber. If you try to install a simple app, which normally doesn't do much, the directions that come with it normally tell you, (with time and trial and error), how to get it working. Even if it ends up running from the wrong place on the PC. Now, take a real app that for example was mentioned above,  amule, the directions are not quite so "clear". Example of this is this (cut)
888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888
Requirements
--------------

  You will need glib/gtk-1.2.10 (package names like glib and glibdev
  or glib-devel, gtk and gtkdev or gtk-devel or similar) or gtk2
  (package names correspond to gtk ones), libexpat (package name
  should be expat) and gettext to compile aMule. Also wxWidgets-2.4.2 or greater (wxGTK-2.6.x is recommended),
  linked against glib/gtk-1.2.10 is needed (package names wxGTK and
  wxGTK-devel or similar).

  If you compile with wxGTK-2.4.2, you will need wxBase-2.4.2
  package,  too, if you want to use amulecmd (the TextClient).
  You can link it to wxgtk too, but it won't run on non-graphical consoles,
  thus removing all the fun ;)
  Since wxWidgets-2.5.x you don't need wxBase anymore.

  It is known to compile in GCC 3.2, 3.3 and 3.4, older GCC's probably 
  can't handle Microsoft C++ well enough.

 How to compile wxWidgets
--------------------------

  Only GTK1 is supported. GTK2 with wxWidgets 2.6 and greater, but it is known
  to have lots of leaks and so is not supported.

  For GTK1:
  ./configure  --prefix=/usr --disable-gtk2 --with-gtk && make

  After wxWidgets has compiled and you have installed it, you can compile aMule.
  Do "./configure && make" as usual. If for some reason, wx-config cannot be 
  found, use ./configure --with-wx-config=/path/wx-config. Sometimes it will be
  named wxgtk-2.4-config.

  To install it, as root type "make install" anyway, you don't have to install
  if you don't want to. It will run fine from the source directory too.

  Note: If you are using a CVS version, you will have to run ./autogen.sh before
  ./configure to generate configure script. Automake > 1.5, Autoconf >= 2.57 and
  gettext are required.
888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888888

This by itself may seem simple to most in the linux field, however from the point of using ubuntu with preloaded app's/ports  TO  the point you know what the hell all that means is not exactly DOC'ed well. And if it is,,, it's busted up so many ways, in so many area's the chances of finding it before your frustration leads you to the top of a water tower somewhere with a SKS is slim to none. 
So, my question is, IS THERE A SITE that someone has FIXED this problem? At least enough to where some of us can learn without asking someONE every min how to do every little thing? And please, don't tell me man pages and wigs. Both expect you to know something to learn anything. Example, if I want to know how to list the files in a directory, unless I already know "man ls" then it kind of useless isn't it? I intend, from a windows, human point of veiw to fix this once I learn it. I will make a windows guide to ubuntu if I have to. I am on a war path here and intend to learn this if it kills me. Please and thank you.
ps, I know you unix/linux people are very defensive about this stuff so I mean no disrespect, I need help and I will help others. (forgive spelling/grammer)-lost my sense of humor along time ago.

---

You want clear help and explanations? Then go to the Menu **System**->**Help**. From there, click **Ubuntu 5.10 Starter Guide**, which Is exactly what you probably want: A starter's guide to Ubuntu which doesn't assume previous knowledge about gnu/linux from the reader. For example, if you click "Installing Applications", you would see the prefered way to install software in ubuntu, is using the "Synaptic Package Manager" (from the System->Admninistration menu). Amule is there, you just may have to enable the universe repository (check that help page).

So, read the help page from the begining, try to understand it, try out what is discussed in it. After you finish, you'll get a good grasp of Ubuntu basics, and all will be clearer.

P.S.-This laptop I'm writting in has got Ubuntu for 6 months now, and never have I had the need to compile a program. So don't be discouraged by those instructions you got with amule, as you won't be needing to do it (much. Unless you want/need unpackaged, recently released software).

Good luck, welcome to ubuntu,

### Post by Grey on 2005-10-24
[QUOTE=TheLuggage]Hello all,

Like others here, I am not new to computers, but I am new to Linux. I am responsible at work for setting up some of our older computers with a Linux installation for the sole purpose of connecting to an IBM mainframe with 3270 emulation. What I need is a console based 3270 emulator that I can install on Ubuntu.

I've searched Google repeatedly, read (bewildering) documentation where ever I could find it, and attended a two day Linux training seminar in the hopes of learning how to do this, all to no avail. The closest to success I came was running an x3270 emulation in an Xwindows environment, but I need to run with just the console if at all possible.

Any help that you guys could provide would really be appreciated.

The Luggage.[/QUOTE]

Well, I just took a look on google, as well as synaptic to see what I could find.

I found Hercules in Synaptic, which apparently emulates an IBM mainframe.  To install it, just do this:

```
sudo apt-get install hercules
```

And it should install automatically.  Another thing I found was [this](http://x3270.bgp.nu/), which is x3270.  I googled for debian packages, and I found [this site](http://fatboy.umng.edu.co/debian/pool/non-free/3/3270/), which has precompiled packages for x3270.  To install those, you would just have to do this:

```
sudo dpkg -i <package-name>.deb
```

Where <package-name> is the name of the package.

[QUOTE=TimAy]is there any equivilant to NetStumbler, a program that will show you what wireless networks are availible around you?[/QUOTE]

### Post by 23meg on 2005-11-06
[QUOTE=philleyblunt]does anyone know where i can go to get driver support for sound cards i use a yamaha dsp 2416 tascam firewire fw1804 and an edirol ur80 
i have managed to get my laptop working under ubuntu but i am strugling to get the soundcards working under rosegarden. and what is a jack server and how would i get that running? any ideas or do i have to sell all my gear ?[/QUOTE]

I'm not sure about Linux support for the cards you mentioned but check out the archives of the linux-audio-dev mailing list (or post there) and you'll most likely  find the answer. Here's the website: [http://www.linuxdj.com/audio/lad/](http://www.linuxdj.com/audio/lad/)

You can think of the JACK audio server as an app that lets other audio apps communicate between each other and with your soundcard; in rougher terms it's the ASIO of the linux audio world. I think it's in the repositories, in the package "jackd". Also check out qjackctl, which is a GUI that will let you set JACK options easily.

---

### Post by xchangingminds on 2005-11-08
[QUOTE=poofyhairguy]One thing that I noticed Ubuntu really needed was a place for newer users to be able to find out what apps to use. I know when I first started Linux less than a year ago, my biggest questions were "where is the Linux winamp" or "what is the Linux version of _______ program." So the purpose of this thread it to make a conversion chart. This will be a work in progress for a long time, so please chime in with good ideas for conversions.  Only open source stuff please, and only the most developed programs in each category so as to not confuse. And nothing that isn't in the main/universe also please. I will also list programs that have Window's or OSX ports since a new user might not have any experiance with OSS).

Windows to Linux Conversion:

In Windows                   ---------                                                          In Ubuntu

Internet Explorer               ---------                                                    Firefox

Microsoft Office                           ---------                                             OpenOffice.org

Winamp                   --------                                                                 Xmms

Photoshop                   ---------                                                             Gimp

AIM, ICQ, MSN, Yahoo!, Jabber, IRC  instant messaging                 ---------                                          Gaim
  
Word Pad (or notepad)                  ---------                                            Gedit

Windows Media Player                        ---------                                       Totem

iTunes                          ---------                                                              -for playing music:
                                                                                    -----------------------------Rhythmbox
                                    ----------------------for iPod Syncing
                                                                               --------------------------------Gtkpod

ID3 tag editor ----------------------- easytag




MIRC                               --------                                                             Xchat

Premiere (Movie Editing)              ---------                                              kino

Bittorado                                     ---------                                              Bittorado
                                                                                                  (don't you love  
                                                                                                   native ports)

Dreamweaver                            ---------                                                 Nvu

CDex                               ----------                                                           Sound Juicer 

Nero                                     --------                                                      Gnomebaker

Outlook Express                   ---------                                    Evolution, Thunderbird

Snood                                     ----------                                                   Frozen-bubble

Partition Magic --------- Gparted

eMule ----------- aMule
Soulseek ------------- Nicotine
DC++ -------------- Valknut
any multitorrent client ------------ Azureus
any download manager --------------- D4X or Gwget
regedit -------------------- gconf 

Adobe Illustrator ------------ Inkscape

Remote Desktop Connection ------------ Terminal Server Client

Windows Explorer ------------- Nautilus

Windows Picture and Fax Viewer ------------ Image Viewer (Eye of GNOME)

Paint ------------- Jdraw

Kubuntu:

Internet Explorer --------- Konqueror

Microsoft Office --------- OpenOffice.org/KOffice

Winamp -------- Amarok (with the small view)

Photoshop --------- Gimp

Aol Instant Messenger --------- Kopete

Word Pad (or notepad) --------- Kwrite

Windows Media Player --------- Kaffeine

iTunes --------- -for playing music:
-----------------------------Amarok
-----------------------------Juk
----------------------for iPod Syncing
--------------------------------Gtkpod

MIRC -------- Xchat

Premiere (Movie Editing) --------- kino

Bittorado --------- Azureus QT/Qtorrent
(don't you love
native ports)

Dreamweaver --------- Nvu

CDex ---------- Kaudiocreator

Nero -------- K3B

Outlook Express --------- KMail

Snood ---------- Frozen-bubble

Partition Magic --------- Qparted

EDIT: Here is a much bigger list on another site for those that don't see what they need here:

[http://www.linuxrsp.ru/win-lin-soft/table-eng.html](http://www.linuxrsp.ru/win-lin-soft/table-eng.html)[/QUOTE]

### Post by AmboyGuy on 2005-11-25
[QUOTE=maxbaggi]Anybody aware of a Linux equivalent of Proxomitron?

Proxomitron is a free, highly flexible, user-configurable, small but very powerful, local HTTP web-filtering proxy
[http://www.proxomitron.info/]("http://www.proxomitron.info/")[/QUOTE]

Privacy enhancing HTTP Proxy
Privoxy is a web proxy with advanced filtering capabilities for
protecting privacy, filtering web page content, managing cookies,
controlling access, and removing ads, banners, pop-ups and other
obnoxious Internet junk. Privoxy has a very flexible configuration
and can be customized to suit individual needs and tastes. Privoxy
has application for both stand-alone systems and multi-user networks.

Privoxy is based on Internet Junkbuster (tm).

 Homepage: [http://www.privoxy.org/](http://www.privoxy.org/)

Available from ubuntu universe. Just apt-get or use synaptic.

### Post by alank on 2005-12-03
RE: Opera on Ubuntu Breezy 
------------------------------------

Hi Muzz, 

Im using Ubuntu 5.10 and  just downloaded opera to check out install,
the file I downloaded is :
   opera_8.51-20051114.6-shared-qt_en_etch_i386.deb

To installed Opera I tried
 % sudo dpkg - i opera_8.51-20051114.6-shared-qt_en_etch_i386.deb

This gave dependency warnings;
=========================
pkg: dependency problems prevent configuration of opera:
 opera depends on xlib6g (>= 3.3.6) | xlibs; however:
  Package xlib6g is not installed.
  Package xlibs is not installed.
 opera depends on libqt3-mt (>= 3.3.4) | libqt3c102-mt (>= 3.3.4); however:
  Package libqt3-mt is not installed.
  Package libqt3c102-mt is not installed.
dpkg: error processing opera (--install):
 dependency problems - leaving unconfigured
============================
So I did 
     % sudo apt-get install xlibs libqt3-mt

This needs  to get 3 MB of data

This facilitated the install of Opera.

For any other issues regarding Opera on Ubuntu Breezy I suggest:

    [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/OperaBrowser](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/OperaBrowser)

 Alan.

### Post by MonsterBox on 2005-12-06
[QUOTE=crazyness003]Does anyone know of an alternative to Flash MX 2004 or better yet Flash 8?[/QUOTE]

Using [Crossover Office]("http://www.codeweavers.com/"), you can get Flash MX to work under Linux.

If you don't want to pay for Xover Office, you can install [WINE]("http://winehq.org/") (which Xover is based on) and "do it yourself".

I know that Flash MX works with the latest WINE/Xover, but I'm not sure about the other two ( 2k4 or 8 ). If you're feeling adventurous, you could install either (both?) and give it a shot.

If I wasn't still in my first week of Linux-land I'd give it a go myself. ;) 

If any of this is wrong, someone wiser than me please feel free to correct. :smile:

---

### Post by Trojan1313 on 2005-12-23
> **Replica]hello  said:**
> 
You forgot "install". :)
sudo apt-get install libstdc++5 :)

A tip, try learning to use aptitude instead. Almost the same syntax as apt-get, and if you remove something it removes unused packages to.

For example, gaim installs the package gaim-data whenever you install gaim, since it's a dependency. But if you remove gaim with apt-get later on, you will still have gaim-data there.
```
**kaminix@Kaminix:~/Source codes/gaim-2.0.0beta1$ sudo apt-get install gaim**
Reading package lists... Done
Building dependency tree... Done
The following extra packages will be installed:
  gaim-data
Suggested packages:
  gnome-panel kicker docker
[b]The following NEW packages will be installed:
  gaim gaim-data[/b]
0 upgraded, 2 newly installed, 0 to remove and 0 not upgraded.
Need to get 0B/1447kB of archives.
After unpacking 12.0MB of additional disk space will be used.
Do you want to continue [Y/n]?

Preconfiguring packages ...
Selecting previously deselected package gaim-data.
(Reading database ... 62557 files and directories currently installed.)
Unpacking gaim-data (from .../gaim-data_1%3a1.5.0-1ubuntu3_all.deb) ...
Selecting previously deselected package gaim.
Unpacking gaim (from .../gaim_1%3a1.5.0-1ubuntu3_i386.deb) ...
Setting up gaim-data (1.5.0-1ubuntu3) ...
Setting up gaim (1.5.0-1ubuntu3) ...

**kaminix@Kaminix:~/Source codes/gaim-2.0.0beta1$ sudo apt-get remove gaim**
Reading package lists... Done
Building dependency tree... Done
[b]The following packages will be REMOVED:
  gaim[/b]
0 upgraded, 0 newly installed, 1 to remove and 0 not upgraded.
Need to get 0B of archives.
After unpacking 2200kB disk space will be freed.
Do you want to continue [Y/n]?
(Reading database ... 62879 files and directories currently installed.)
Removing gaim ...
**kaminix@Kaminix:~/Source codes/gaim-2.0.0beta1$ sudo aptitude search gaim**
c   gaim                                                                             - multi-protocol instant messaging client
v   gaim-common                                                                      -
**idA gaim-data**                                                                        - multi-protocol instant messaging client - data files
p   gaim-dev                                                                         - multi-protocol instant messaging client - development files
p   gaim-encryption                                                                  - gaim plugin that provides transparent encryption
p   gaim-extendedprefs                                                               - extended preferences plugin for the instant messenger gaim
v   gaim-gnome                                                                       -
p   gaim-guifications                                                                - toaster popups for gaim
p   gaim-irchelper                                                                   - IRC extensions for GAIM
p   gaim-meanwhile                                                                   - gaim plugin for Meanwhile
p   gaim-otr                                                                         - Off-the-Record Messaging plugin for gaim
p   gaim-themes                                                                      - Smiley themes collection for gaim

```
I highlighted the lines I thought you should pay attention to. The i next to gaim-data in the last highlight means "installed".

EDIT 1:
Don't be confused about the ~/Source Codes/gaim-2.0.0beta1 thingie, I've just failed in compiling the new gaim-beta. :p Hence the reason why gaim was the first program that came to mind when making an example. :)

EDIT 2:
[QUOTE=patrick295767][COLOR="Black"][SIZE="3"]**W**[/SIZE][/COLOR]hat 's the best programs to make use of your webcam (chat & pictures & videos) ?

thank you !
  
Patrick
The gaim-2.0.0beta1 can handle webcams in MSN. It's not entierly easy to get it working though.
You need gnutls, speex and some other things I don't know the name of.

When (if you decide to try it) compiling gaim 2.0.0-beta1, type ./configure --help to see available options and stuff (turn on everything you want, run ./configure and it'll tell you what you're missing, then google for the missing things and install them).

MSN users need to configure gaim with the option --enable-gnutls=yes to be able to log in. If you don't have this option MSN won't work.

Hi and very welcome

to download : [http://www.ubuntulinux.org/download](http://www.ubuntulinux.org/download)

you have the choice between a "live cd" and an "install cd"

the "live cd" lets you try Ubuntu without installing anything
the "install cd" installs Ubuntu on your system,

### Post by estel on 2006-01-05
[QUOTE=Nightwind]Hi
As a new linux user, but not new to computers as a whole one of the main issues for me as well as other I am sure is compiling.
I have not seen (perhaps over looked it) a "How to compile basics" on the forums. I've seen many instructions on compiling for specific hardware/software. 
The main questions I have are: 
What programs do you use to compile in Ubuntu 5.10? I'm sure that there are certain compiling programs that work with some distros and not with others. 
So if I needed to compile say Gnokii for an examle how would I do that?
Some programs have to have code for lack of a better term to get them to work with certain programs and hardware. I understand that it would be impossible to have a "How to for every piece of hardware/software" but it would make it less daunting to have some step by step instructions on basic beginner compiling.
I  am happy with 5.10 so far after looking at other distros and trying a few and have even attempted to get my family members to use it. But they have run into the same issues I have which is where to start?
Thanks!
Trish :confused:[/QUOTE]

Noone answered this?

Generally, you'll download a tar ball of the source code. This is almost entirely system independent, and only in rare cicrumstances (ish) will it not compile.
After extracting the tar ball, read the README. Make sure that you've installed any dependencies using apt-get (usually lots of -dev packages) or compile them, if they're not available.
Open the folder in the terminal. Type ```
./configure
``` You might get a few questions, you might not, but as long as you don't get any error messages (which can generally be fixed) wait for it to finish and then type ```
make
```.

Done that? Type ```
make install
``` if it's the sort of thing that you need to install. To be honest, that is *all* that there is to it.

Oh, you will need to install build-essentials first from the repositories.

### Post by Rinzwind on 2006-01-08
cgc: did you installed gnome? 
- In applications you have an 'add packages'. It's ticking a box and hit install.
Tho it'd limited to what can be installed.

- There's synaptic inside system/administration/synaptic package manager
(kde has kynaptic btw). Works perfectly. But don't forget to open universe and multiverse (check: [http://ubuntuguide.org/](http://ubuntuguide.org/))

### Post by christooss on 2006-01-16
Software has to be build properly. For exemple Exe files wont work on linux even though it is open source.

On Ubuntu you can install .deb packages through apt-get or dpkg -i. Of course you can build your self packages from source <--- This is THA OPEN SOURCE :)

You can run exe files through Wine

### Post by browndog on 2006-01-17
PHG,

Excellent and helpful list for a new Ubuntu user...thanks much!

[QUOTE=poofyhairguy]One thing that I noticed Ubuntu really needed was a place for newer users to be able to find out what apps to use. I know when I first started Linux less than a year ago, my biggest questions were "where is the Linux winamp" or "what is the Linux version of _______ program." So the purpose of this thread it to make a conversion chart. This will be a work in progress for a long time, so please chime in with good ideas for conversions.  Only open source stuff please, and only the most developed programs in each category so as to not confuse. And nothing that isn't in the main/universe also please. I will also list programs that have Window's or OSX ports since a new user might not have any experiance with OSS).

Windows to Linux Conversion:

In Windows                   ---------                                                          In Ubuntu

Internet Explorer               ---------                                                    Firefox

Microsoft Office                           ---------                                             OpenOffice.org

Winamp                   --------                                                                 Xmms

Photoshop                   ---------                                                             Gimp

AIM, ICQ, MSN, Yahoo!, Jabber, IRC  instant messaging                 ---------                                          Gaim
  
Word Pad (or notepad)                  ---------                                            Gedit

Windows Media Player                        ---------                                       Totem

iTunes                          ---------                                                              -for playing music:
                                                                                    -----------------------------Rhythmbox
                                    ----------------------for iPod Syncing
                                                                               --------------------------------Gtkpod

MIRC                               --------                                                             Xchat

                                                                                                  (don't you love  
                                                                                                   native ports)

Dreamweaver                            ---------                                                 Nvu

CDex                               ----------                                                           Sound Juicer

Snood                                     ----------                                                   Frozen-bubble

Soulseek ------------- Nicotine

any multitorrent client ------------ Azureus
any download manager --------------- D4X or Gwget
regedit -------------------- gconf

### Post by roseynose on 2006-02-21
Audio Editing:
Windows: CoolEdit Pro/Adobe (or other audio editing software)
Mac: Protools
Linux: Audacity

CD/DVD Burning:
Windows: Nero or Roxio
Linux: K3B or Nautilus

Video Editing:
Windows: Adobe Premiere or Pinaccle or Windows MovieMaker
Linux: kfilm or Kdenlive or Jahshaka

TV Watching:
Windows: WinTV, ATI, etc......
Linux: btv, kdetv, or tvtime

Solitaire (yes, solitaire is still important to some people):
Windows: Solitaire, Freecell
Linux: PySol, XPat, Patience

### Post by Trojan1313 on 2006-03-02

if you want php5:
sudo aptitude install php5

if you want mysql:
sudo aptitude install mysql-server
sudo aptitude install libapache2-mod-auth-mysql

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-03-03
shadow: Type those commands into the Terminal application that is provided with Ubuntu. The commands download and install Apache, PHP and MySQL, and automatically set them up to work with eachother.

pcwebber: As far as getting your hands on a Live CD, you can download an ISO from [www.ubuntu.com](www.ubuntu.com). Alternatively, you can order one from ShipIt ([https://shipit.ubuntu.com)](https://shipit.ubuntu.com)), but it'll take a few weeks and will extract a little bit of money from a nice guy's bank account.

I highly recommend using Ubuntu to put a bit of life into a computer that does run the latest proprietry OSes. I'm doing it right now :-)

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2006-03-08
[QUOTE=Rasymas]Greetings people,

does anyone knows what program should I use in order to burn cds/dvds ? I've tried gnomebaker, but i couldn't install it.. smth ain't right.. any solutions? You can advice me some other program though :)

Thanks in advance ;)[/QUOTE]

To install gnomebaker you need to enable "universe" in your sourcelist.
This is how you do it:
Open your terminal: Applications ---> Accessories ---> Terminal
(you can also right click the terminal to add it to your panel for easy access)

type:
```
sudo gedit /etc/apt/sources.list
```

Remove the "#" that is infront of the lines. Except where there's two of ##. (recheck if you got them all)
Save it and close it.
Back to terminal and type:
```
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install gnomebaker

```

As I recall it gnomebaker launcher will show up in application ---> Accessories.


Another options is to get Kb3 but it needs kde libs to work.

You can also try with nerolinux: [http://www.nero.com/en/NeroLINUX.html](http://www.nero.com/en/NeroLINUX.html)
if you have serial code for nero 6 or higher you can use the serial code to activate full version of nero linux.

### Post by m.musashi on 2006-03-08
Well, that's easy enough:). I guess I was thinking of packages that are in the form tar.gz. I remember trying to add the latest firefox (before I found automatix) and couldn't figure it out. Could you point me to a tutorial for those types of packages?

Thanks.

---

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2006-03-08
[QUOTE=m.musashi]Well, that's easy enough:). I guess I was thinking of packages that are in the form tar.gz. I remember trying to add the latest firefox (before I found automatix) and couldn't figure it out. Could you point me to a tutorial for those types of packages?

Thanks.[/QUOTE]
Simplified version

You mean source?
tar.gz is just a compressed file something like .zip.
Sometimes you'll also find Dynamic and static binaries. Dynamic binaries needs share libs and other stuff installed to work. Static binaries comes with their own libs, and works out of the box but static binary programs take up more resources instead of dynamic as it runs it own libs next to your share libs (like in windows). Dynamic use your share libs, but doesn't install the "right" way but run from the folder you extracted it to.

source:
I couldn't find a good place where it explain about source (anyone who can provide a good link?) but the default is something like:
extract the tar.gz
./configure
make
sudo make install
but it all depends which programs it uses (jam, automake etc.). A very good idea is to read the readme and/or their homepage for more information.

Edit: I have written this for gaming, check wher it says packeges: [http://doc.gwos.org/index.php/Native_Games_Userguide](http://doc.gwos.org/index.php/Native_Games_Userguide)

---

You just have to add them to your path and some stuff like that, tricky if you don't know the folder hierachy.

### Post by biktor on 2006-03-09
hi, where I get an antivirus for ubuntu??

---

### Post by Brunellus on 2006-03-09
[QUOTE=biktor]hi, where I get an antivirus for ubuntu??[/QUOTE]
not needed, generally.  ClamAV (in the universe repositories) will do, but it's mainly meant to be run on mailservers to protect windows users using the same network.

For a more systematic treatment about viruses in linux see the link below:

[http://linuxmafia.com/~rick/faq/index.php?page=virus#virus](http://linuxmafia.com/~rick/faq/index.php?page=virus#virus)

the lesson:  do NOT run as root unnecessarily, and you will be OK.

---

### Post by tuxcantfly on 2006-03-19
For the opera installation, the deb package seems to have bad dependency information. You can get rid of this by converting it to rpm and then back. First get alien:

sudo apt-get install alien

Then convert it to rpm:

sudo alien -R /path/to/operaversion.deb

It should generate some rpm file, then convert it back:

sudo alien /path/to/operaversion.rpm

It should generate another deb file. Install it:

sudo dpkg -i /path/to/operanewversion.deb

### Post by tuxinvader on 2006-03-21
[QUOTE=Apollyein]I'm trying to hunt down Gtelnet or a similar program, but am having trouble finding a working download. I have found two similar programs, but they tell me to "make install" and I have no idea what that means. Can anyone help?

~Polly[/QUOTE]
"make install" is how you install a software package from source. Usually there will be a README or INSTALL file in the archive once you have unpacked it. Presumably you downloaded a source archive *.tbz or *.tgz?

Extract the source using (zxvf) for gz or (jxvf) for bzip2
   $ tar zxvf package.tgz

Move into the new unpacked directory
   $ cd package-dir

Read the README or INSTALL file, but usually the sequence is:

   $ ./configure
   $ make
   $ sudo make install

The first line detects your system settings and creates an appropriate make file. The second line builds the application and the third installs it.

---

### Post by Apollyein on 2006-03-22
[QUOTE=tuxinvader]"make install" is how you install a software package from source. Usually there will be a README or INSTALL file in the archive once you have unpacked it. Presumably you downloaded a source archive *.tbz or *.tgz?

Extract the source using (zxvf) for gz or (jxvf) for bzip2
   $ tar zxvf package.tgz

Move into the new unpacked directory
   $ cd package-dir

Read the README or INSTALL file, but usually the sequence is:

   $ ./configure
   $ make
   $ sudo make install

The first line detects your system settings and creates an appropriate make file. The second line builds the application and the third installs it.[/QUOTE]
Thanks a bunch!

~Polly

### Post by barfos on 2006-03-26
sudo make install
will place the binaries and configuration files for the app in various system folders for all users to use.  One gotcha: If you wish to remove the app, you either type
sudo make uninstall
if the developer provided that target in the makefile, or you have to go find all those files and remove them manually if he didn't.  

Avoid this by getting a program called "checkinstall" from synaptic.  Instead of doing make install, do

sudo checkinstall

at that point.  This will create a debian package out of your source.  If it doesn't autoinstall the package for you, just do

sudo dpkg -i [packagename.deb]

This has the advantage of easily removing the application later.  Just use synaptic for that. You can also get rid of the source for the app, as its not needed anymore.

---

### Post by openmind on 2006-04-01

### Post by AndrewCaul on 2006-04-03
[QUOTE=danielhendry]so if I log on as an user? what the different between just user with owner?
coz I tried to make folder codec on \usr\lib\codecs but the "make new folder" is grey..

I read from the readme files of mplayer codec that I should make that folder and copy all files there... should I do that or not? coz my totem just can't play .mp3...

You can use **sudo programname** or **gksudo programname** to run a program as root.
I think you can use **gksudo nautilus**, then create the folder and copy the files.

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2006-04-15
.exe is a windows format.
To might check this first: [Ubuntu restricted]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/RestrictedFormats")

You don't have to download packages from diffrent places.
Go to System tab ---> Adminstration ---> Synaptic package manager
Everything is gathered under one roof (in most cases).
Also you can use the command line to install remove etc. programs:
eg.
```
sudo apt-get install mplayer-i386
```

### Post by fyrestrtr on 2006-04-23
[QUOTE=Replica]I want chanhe my source.list file but it's problem with "kate" :p 
here it is:

1700693 Desktop  1700673 sylfaen

1700693 Desktop  1700673 sylfaen

2894329 apt.conf.d   2894784 sources.list  2894744 trusted.gpg
2894739 secring.gpg  2894742 trustdb.gpg   2894741 trusted.gpg~
root@ubuntu:/etc/apt# sudo kate sources.list
Xlib: connection to ":0.0" refused by server
Xlib: No protocol specified
 
kded: cannot connect to X server :0.0
kded: ERROR: KUniqueApplication: Registering failed!
kded: ERROR: Communication problem with kded, it probably crashed.
Xlib: connection to ":0.0" refused by server
Xlib: No protocol specified
 
kdeinit: Can't connect to the X Server.
kdeinit: Might not terminate at end of session.
Xlib: connection to ":0.0" refused by server
Xlib: No protocol specified
 
kate: cannot connect to X server :0.0
DCOP aborting call from 'anonymous-6936' to 'kate'
kate: ERROR: Communication problem with kate, it probably crashed.
root@ubuntu:/etc/apt#

is it anyone who knows whats goin on? thnks much[/QUOTE]

Your X server is not running.  You need to either start it, or use a command line editor, like vi or pine.  You also don't need to do 'sudo' since you are already root.

### Post by Rinzwind on 2006-04-27
Does Ubuntu have something like doublevision? (Doublevision let's you take over another tty through telnet).

[http://www.tridia.com/products/dv.html](http://www.tridia.com/products/dv.html)

    *  Remotely view/control UNIX/Linux consoles, Telnet & tty sessions
    * Support for most UNIX/Linux operating systems
    * Record and playback
    * Terminal translation allows viewing of most terminal types
    * View log provides audit trail of activity
    * Complete access control & password protection
    * Screen blanking
    * Chat
    * File Transfer
    * Dial-up, Network and Internet connection support
    * Encrypted connections
    * View UNIX or Linux servers behind firewalls
    * Telnet with robust emulation 


It costs 495 dollars for a single processor and that's way to expensive.

### Post by Rinzwind on 2006-04-28

What this program does is the following:

I log in as root.

I open 1 of those tty's and take over his/her session.

Isn't ssh a protocol (like telnet)?

### Post by m.musashi on 2006-04-28
[QUOTE=Rinzwind]Not exactly.

What this program does is the following:

I log in as root.
Start dv and get a list of ttynrs that are present in that system.
I open 1 of those tty's and take over his/her session.

Isn't ssh a protocol (like telnet)?[/QUOTE]
Real VNC allows you to talk over another's session. Would that be similar to what you are looking for? Check out [http://www.realvnc.com/](http://www.realvnc.com/). There is even a wiki that describes how to use VNC over SSH for a more secure takeover [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/VNCOverSSH](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/VNCOverSSH).

Hope that helps.

### Post by sha_man on 2006-04-29
[QUOTE=ZelasMetallium]Is there a program that rips CDs to mp3 format?  I've tried those you say are like iTunes in the first post but I can't seem to find how to make them rip as mp3.[/QUOTE]
Try *Grip*, it's excellent, **BEST CD-RIPPER FOR LINUX**! Have a look at this HowTo: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=99115&highlight=grip+howto](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=99115&highlight=grip+howto) ;)


Addition to the 1st post:

*Windows/Mac*: 
- iTunes

*Linux*:

Linux has some good music players or at least WILL have...

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-05-01
[QUOTE=sha_man]Try *Grip*, it's excellent, **BEST CD-RIPPER FOR LINUX**! Have a look at this HowTo: [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=99115&highlight=grip+howto](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=99115&highlight=grip+howto) ;)[/QUOTE]

I also highly recommend Grip. It is the only program that successfully plays CDs in my computer, too.

As for the question about how to get Nautilus to behave like NeXT (sorry... OS X), the new version of Nautilus does not have this type of view, and I don't think any of the most popular file managers have it. However, you might want to try doing a search on Synaptic for "file manager" and try out a few.

### Post by kanndragons on 2006-05-27
I am playing a game ishar ATM and need to download a mud client i have downloaded one called mcl and it opens.. in the read me it shows this message.

Basic Installation
==================

   These are generic installation instructions.

   The `configure' shell script attempts to guess correct values for
various system-dependent variables used during compilation.  It uses
those values to create a `Makefile' in each directory of the package.
It may also create one or more `.h' files containing system-dependent
definitions.  Finally, it creates a shell script `config.status' that
you can run in the future to recreate the current configuration, a file
`config.cache' that saves the results of its tests to speed up
reconfiguring, and a file `config.log' containing compiler output
(useful mainly for debugging `configure').

   If you need to do unusual things to compile the package, please try
to figure out how `configure' could check whether to do them, and mail
diffs or instructions to the address given in the `README' so they can
be considered for the next release.  If at some point `config.cache'
contains results you don't want to keep, you may remove or edit it.

   The file `configure.in' is used to create `configure' by a program
called `autoconf'.  You only need `configure.in' if you want to change
it or regenerate `configure' using a newer version of `autoconf'.

The simplest way to compile this package is:

  1. `cd' to the directory containing the package's source code and type
     `./configure' to configure the package for your system.  If you're
     using `csh' on an old version of System V, you might need to type
     `sh ./configure' instead to prevent `csh' from trying to execute
     `configure' itself.

     Running `configure' takes awhile.  While running, it prints some
     messages telling which features it is checking for.

  2. Type `make' to compile the package.

  3. Type `make install' to install the programs and any data files and
     documentation.

  4. You can remove the program binaries and object files from the
     source code directory by typing `make clean'.  To also remove the
     files that `configure' created (so you can compile the package for
     a different kind of computer), type `make distclean'.

Compilers and Options
=====================

   Some systems require unusual options for compilation or linking that
the `configure' script does not know about.  You can give `configure'
initial values for variables by setting them in the environment.  Using
a Bourne-compatible shell, you can do that on the command line like
this:
     CC=c89 CFLAGS=-O2 LIBS=-lposix ./configure

Or on systems that have the `env' program, you can do it like this:
     env CPPFLAGS=-I/usr/local/include LDFLAGS=-s ./configure

Compiling For Multiple Architectures
====================================

   You can compile the package for more than one kind of computer at the
same time, by placing the object files for each architecture in their
own directory.  To do this, you must use a version of `make' that
supports the `VPATH' variable, such as GNU `make'.  `cd' to the
directory where you want the object files and executables to go and run
the `configure' script.  `configure' automatically checks for the
source code in the directory that `configure' is in and in `..'.

   If you have to use a `make' that does not supports the `VPATH'
variable, you have to compile the package for one architecture at a time
in the source code directory.  After you have installed the package for
one architecture, use `make distclean' before reconfiguring for another
architecture.

Installation Names
==================

   By default, `make install' will install the package's files in
`/usr/local/bin', `/usr/local/man', etc.  You can specify an
installation prefix other than `/usr/local' by giving `configure' the
option `--prefix=PATH'.

   In addition, if you want to use a install root different from /,
you may specify that by giving `configure' the option
`--with-install-root=PATH'.

Optional Features
=================

   `configure' recognizes the following options to choose wheter to
enable or not a specific feature.

`--enable-perl', `--enable-perl=PATH' and `--disable-perl'
   Enable perl support, optionally telling configure where to find it,
or simply disable perl.

`--enable-python', `--enable-python=PATH' and `--disable-python'
   Enable python support, optionally telling configure where to find it,
or simply disable python.

`--enable-debug' and `--disable-debug'
   Enable or disable debug support.

`--enable-efence' and `--disable-efence'
   Enable or disable support for the Electric Fence malloc debugger.

Specifying the System Type
==========================

   There may be some features `configure' can not figure out
automatically, but needs to determine by the type of host the package
will run on.  Usually `configure' can figure that out, but if it prints
a message saying it can not guess the host type, give it the
`--host=TYPE' option.  TYPE can either be a short name for the system
type, such as `sun4', or a canonical name with three fields:
     CPU-COMPANY-SYSTEM

See the file `config.sub' for the possible values of each field.  If
`config.sub' isn't included in this package, then this package doesn't
need to know the host type.

Operation Controls
==================

   `configure' recognizes the following options to control how it
operates.

`--cache-file=FILE'
     Use and save the results of the tests in FILE instead of
     `./config.cache'.  Set FILE to `/dev/null' to disable caching, for
     debugging `configure'.

`--help'
     Print a summary of the options to `configure', and exit.

`--quiet'
`--silent'
`-q'
     Do not print messages saying which checks are being made.  To
     suppress all normal output, redirect it to `/dev/null' (any error
     messages will still be shown).

`--srcdir=DIR'
     Look for the package's source code in directory DIR.  Usually
     `configure' can determine that directory automatically.

`--version'
     Print the version of Autoconf used to generate the `configure'
     script, and exit.

`configure' also accepts some other, not widely useful, options.

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-05-28
[QUOTE=kanndragons]I am playing a game ishar ATM and need to download a mud client i have downloaded one called mcl and it opens.. in the read me it shows this message.

<snip>

As i am BRAND NEW to this i have no idea what it's tlaking about could you put it in easy steps on how to install it??[/QUOTE]

Go into a terminal by going "Applications > Accessories > Terminal". Type "sudo apt-get install build-essential", and hit Enter. This installs the compiling utilities.

Now you will need to navigate in the terminal to the unpacked directory (the one which Archive Manager created when you unzipped the archive). If you don't know how to do that:

1. Type ls and hit Enter. It shows you a list of files and directories inside the current directory. Decide which directory you want to move into.

2. Type cd directoryname, where directoryname is the name of the directory you want to move into. Press Enter.

3. Repeat until you are inside the appropriate directory.

Now, type "./configure" without the quotes, and press Enter. Hopefully, the configuration process will complete successfully. Now type "make" and Enter. If you're really lucky, the program will compile successfully. If you're a little less lucky, it will tell you that you need a particular development library. If you do, go to Synaptic Package Manager and install it. E.g. if it says you need libfoo, you would install libfoo-dev.

When compilation is complete (it will take a while), type "sudo make install" (without the quotes).

Compiling software is not something anyone recommends for new users. I've been using Linux for 6 months and I sometimes can't get software to compile. If you have trouble, either live without the program until you have a better knowledge of Linux, find a precompiled binary (a .deb file is best, but you can use a .rpm as well), or ask around to see if anyone else has compiled that software before and can make you a .deb.

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2006-05-29
[QUOTE=davereid]Hi all,

Like SirCoistrel, I'm not new to computers, I can bash my way away around a windows PC ok. But I wanted to install Opera. Hmm on windows, I click download, it downloads then I need to click install, job done. I downloaded Opera on Ubuntu, and promptly lost the plot. Had the download, but got lost thereafter... 

I don't want to be stuck with windoze Vista ! please help me to learn the basics of installing, running and if they are dogs deleting apps in Ubuntu !

(Dumb Bu55er but happy to learn !)

Which version of Ubuntu do you use? Are you using Gnome or KDE Desktop or other?
Did you downloaded a .deb package? If so, open the terminal (in Gnome = Application tab ---> Accessories ---> terminal) and write
```
cd /where/thepackage/is
sudo dpkg -i XXXXXXXXX.deb
```

The **cd** is to browser through folders etc. to the right path. Eg. If the package is on your Desktop: **cd Desktop**, if you save it in a sub-folder in you home folder **cd /home/<youname>/my-downloads**
sudo gives you **superuser do**, dpkg is the application to install independent downloaded .deb package,  the -i means install. XXXXXXXXXX.deb name of the package.

### Post by vidak on 2006-05-30
[QUOTE=kanndragons]Do you have a link for synaptic?? and what is it? 


](*,) ](*,) ](*,) ](*,) ](*,)[/QUOTE]

you could use aptitude, too...
open a console, and just enter "aptitude", then hit F1 for a short help...

Don't forget, that sometimes it could be necessary to compile a software from source. It is a good idea to do it first just 'for fun', so next time you would REALLY need it, you know more about it... I would recommend  a small and simple program (like eg wmdl).
The main thing is really easy: unzip the tarball, then
./configure
make
sudo make install

or use 
sudo checkinstall 
instead of the last one - this will make a deb package and install it...
Good luck!

### Post by justinflavin on 2006-06-05
[QUOTE=Maupertus]As I have no experience whatsoever with Xfce and am now using Xubuntu to blow new life into my old box (succesfully I might add) I was wondering if there are certain prog's and app's native or just better suited to Xubuntu. 

I know that in prinicple anything will work, but it would be nice to keep this speed.[/QUOTE]

if you are willing to experiment , take a look at Damn Small Linux (and other small distros)  and have a look at the software that they include  - see if you can grab the source code for the apps in questions  and compile them into your lightweight Xubuntu system.

One thing i couldnt find on the Ubuntu repositories was "Siag" - which is an ultra small, and lightweight spreadsheet program - and its quite frankly astonishing how much the developers have packed into that one.

[http://siag.nu/siag/](http://siag.nu/siag/)


Word of warning - compiling your own stuff means that you are breaking away from the apt-get upgrade stuff of Ubuntu and you might get problems later on (you might have to do a fresh install). you are literally creating your own customised version of Ubuntu.

but if you want to experiment, and have a play,theres nothing stopping you.

damn small
[http://www.damnsmalllinux.org/](http://www.damnsmalllinux.org/)

puppy linux
[http://www.puppylinux.org/](http://www.puppylinux.org/)

feather
[http://featherlinux.berlios.de/](http://featherlinux.berlios.de/)

Nothing on Linux can convert a video file to wmv or real media - they're proprietry and completely closed source.

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2006-06-19
[QUOTE=mourad]CarpKing, christooss, Malta Soron and tronica , thank you guys for your help ... But still talking about programs, I did not notice anyone talking about antivirus and anti spyware programs ??? Is this because Linux so impentratable and secure ??? or is it because the hackers and virus people are busy hacking and impaling the windows :) .....!!![/QUOTE]

Well, there several reason why:
1. Linux is more secure by default compared to windows default.
2. Linux doesn't use activeX (The Devil invented it).
3. Not so many Linux users vs. Windows users.
4. the user with a evil-script have to make it executionable and then run afterwards as root to effect his/her system.
5. Open Source: Everyone can see what exactly the script/application etc. do.
6. Usually people get download software/lib/etc. from the sourcelist/repo so the procent to get infected is almost 0.
7. Faster security fixes and updates.

But as said (the person above me) you can get  AVG for linux though I'll recommend F-prot. These a good for scanning/removing bad things from your windows PCs, scanning mail, servers, networking with windows. Otherwise there's no need for it:
Howto F-prot - [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=88357](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=88357)
Howto AVG - [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=136064](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=136064)

---

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2006-06-21
If you can't find a program/application you installed in ubuntu/linux, use the command; **locate** or **whereis**

eg.
whereis mplayer

locate mplayer

Usually something will show up in /usr/bin /usr/share/bin etc. which are the file to launch the application. Just write that file name in the terminal to start the application. If successed...You can make a launcher for it if you like.



You can get some Windows stuff running on Ubuntu/linux, with wine or crossover office, but don't expect to much. Wine can be pretty hard to set right up for a specific windows program if you havn't tried it before. Best solution is to find a program in linux which do the same thing you're looking for.

---

### Post by Shampyon on 2006-07-01
You need to be online. Go to Applications>Add/Remove Programs and you'll find a lot of stuff there. If what you're looking for isn't there, choose Advanced, you go to the Synaptic Package Manager. Go to Settings>Repositories, and select the repositories marked Main, Universe, Multiverse and Restricted. You can search for VLC with the search function thru Synaptic.

If it's not there, try out Automatix:
[http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=177646](http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=177646)

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-07-06
[QUOTE=ELD]I am just wondering if there is any point-and-click software/game creation program available for linux.

For an example look at the products of [www.clickteam.com](www.clickteam.com) (TGF, MMF, TGF2, MMF2 etc etc).[/QUOTE]

[http://www.runrev.com/](http://www.runrev.com/)

Revolution Studio would be the kind of thing you're looking for. It's based on the Metacard engine, which in turn is a modern clone of Hypercard. Unfortunately, Revolution is not cost-free and it seems like Metacard is no longer available.

Also, before you shell out the big bucks, Revolution is a general purpose multimedia authoring program; so in order to write games you would have to learn its internal scripting language, which is very easy. Think Macromedia Director.

---

### Post by ALIENDUDE5300 on 2006-07-06
[QUOTE=poofyhairguy]Outlook Express --------- KMail[/QUOTE]
I think That Outlook Express Should Be Mozilla Thunderbird because Thunderbird is simple to use and total noobs might be familiar with the Windows Version, unlike KMail which is only for linux. Also, Thunderbird is more customizable with themes such as [Tiger Mail]("https://addons.mozilla.org/thunderbird/1713/") and [WinMail]("https://addons.mozilla.org/thunderbird/2523/") plus extensons that can increase Functionality, such as [Enigmail]("https://addons.mozilla.org/thunderbird/71/"). Thunderbird has powerful features and support for many types of email. Thunderbird also has Advanced Security and Automatic Updates to keep itself at the latest version.

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-07-07
> **crystal said:**
> Any chance that Wine would work with sibelius? If it does then your problem would be solved right away... though you would still have to buy it.

Wine might work, but it wouldn't be able to output MIDI events to a keyboard, and it probably wouldn't be able to generate sounds internally from the MIDI.

Have you looked at NoteEdit or RoseGarden 4? Both are KDE-based programs, but NoteEdit doesn't really rely on many KDE dependencies.

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-07-08
> **'[-Ghost-] said:**
> This thread is great for helpin me weed out my windows dependant software needs. I just installed Kubuntu a week ago but am still dual-booting with Windows XP til i get the last few programs replaced. One of my remaining needed programs is a replacement for Easy Video Capture, that i use for making avi files of webcam conferences. Anyone know of a linux program that does this? I've yet to try Easy Video Capture in Wine, i guess i could always poke around with that if there are no other options.

Thanks

WINE doesn't tend to like programs that try to access hardware directly. A program that uses a webcam is probably likely to be one of those programs that won't work. But try it anyway.

To the previous poster: When you say "draw interfaces", which programming language do you want to use? Which interface toolkit?

I haven't tried Glade, but I hear that it's good for GTK GUIs with C and C++. If you want to write in Python, try Pythoncard. If you want to do multimedia programming, try Runtime Revolution (not cost-free).
