[QUOTE="http://www.erightsoft.com/faqt.html"]SUPER © is a GUI for major Command line encoders that are initially written for Linux.
SUPER © was released because there was no existing GUI running on Windows© for those encoders.
It is useless to write a version of SUPER © for Linux as there are already many Linux GUI for those encoders.

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-07-11
Shampyon, what command-line program did you want a GUI for? There tend to be different GUI frontends for different programs; sometimes with Ubuntu the frontend will come with the program.

Try searching on Sourceforge.net for "*appname* frontend", where *appname* is the name of the command-line program. (for instance, lame frontend).

Otherwise, you could just bite the bullet and use the command line. Most of the time, it's not difficult to do as long as you have the manual in front of you.

---

### Post by Shampyon on 2006-07-12

### Post by Kjersten on 2006-07-16
When I had Windows, I used openCanvas exclusively as my image editor, and when I switched, I forgot to save my work as .jpg files instead of just .oci files. Does anyone happen to know of a way to convert .oci files to a file type acceptable to the GIMP?

---

### Post by SqRt7744 on 2006-07-16
> **Kjersten said:**
> When I had Windows, I used openCanvas exclusively as my image editor, and when I switched, I forgot to save my work as .jpg files instead of just .oci files. Does anyone happen to know of a way to convert .oci files to a file type acceptable to the GIMP?

I don't know if that particular file format is supported by Imagemagick, but for the file formats supported by it (which include very many types, including pdf, gif, jpg, png... etc), you convert by typing at the terminal
(for example, from jpg to png)

convert inputfile.jpg outputfile.png

don't forget to first:
sudo apt-get install imagemagick

---

### Post by Kjersten on 2006-07-16

> I don't know if that particular file format is supported by Imagemagick, but for the file formats supported by it (which include very many types, including pdf, gif, jpg, png... etc), you convert by typing at the terminal
(for example, from jpg to png)

convert inputfile.jpg outputfile.png

don't forget to first:
sudo apt-get install imagemagick

bash: syntax error near unexpected token `('

### Post by SqRt7744 on 2006-07-17
> **Kjersten said:**
> bash: syntax error near unexpected token `('
I have very little command line experience, but I assume that means that imagemagick doesn't support .oci files. Err.. right? Anyway, thank you for your suggestion:)

You might be out of luck with the .oci files.  It seems that oC had a free but not open source version, now it is closed source software.  I'm guessing they haven't released the specs for their oci file format, and thus there are no tools to convert it to a different format.  Some people run oC under linux using wine, maybe you could try that - or use opencanvas on a windows box to save the files in a different format.

I might be wrong about this, it was just based on a 5 mins of internet research.  If anyone knows better please share...

### Post by fatsheep on 2006-07-18
On windows I have all sorts of security applications: firewalls, anti-spyware, anti-virus, anti-trojan, etc...  Is it necessary to get security applications for ubuntu or am I pretty secure already?

---

### Post by Sonic Alpha on 2006-07-18
> **fatsheep said:**
> On windows I have all sorts of security applications: firewalls, anti-spyware, anti-virus, anti-trojan, etc...  Is it necessary to get security applications for ubuntu or am I pretty secure already?

Virus software isn't really necessary with Linux, unless you're running a mail server (which serves windows machines).  The only Linux viruses that exist, are not "in the wild", so you have nothing to worry about.

Current spyware targets Windows only.

When you installed Ubuntu, it came with a built in firewall.  You just need to install the graphical frontend, which is called "Firestarter", I believe.

However, if you're sat behind a decent router, that (along with the built in firewall) is apparently enough.

---

Current spyware targets Windows only.

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-07-19
> **frozen_yak said:**
> Hi all

I am new to ubuntu (yet to install), but i have a fairly decent knowledge of computing. As far as i know, rhythmbox can play mp4 and can sync with my ipod. my entire music collection is in mp4 format and i was wondering what my option are regarding playing my music on ubuntu. also, is it possible with dapper drake to somehow transfer my music collection from windows to ubuntu without having to back it up?

cheers

Rhythmbox can play MP4 as long as you have the gstreamer Mp4 plugin and the file is not encrypted (i.e. it doesn't come from an online music store).

You can transfer your music collection from Windows to Ubuntu when you mount your existing Windows partition... however, if your partition is mounted, then you don't really need to transfer the files across. You will almost certainly have to re-create your existing playlists if any, as the files will be in different locations when running Ubuntu.

(that last sentence probably won't make sense to you at first... but trust me on it)

---

cheers

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-07-20
> **frozen_yak said:**
> Ok thanks for that...I'm not really up with all this partition stuff though, how do i create a partition which protects my music, and other important files? thanks for ur help mate 

do you have a link for the plug in i need?

cheers

You don't need to create any partitions other than the ones Ubuntu sets up for you. You can set up the system to "mount" (make available) the partition that Windows and your existing MP3s sit on. Then you can access those files just like you would any other disk. PM me if/when you install Ubuntu and I'll send you a script to automatically mount your Windows partition.

To install the plugins, please follow these instructions:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/ubuntu/desktopguide/C/extra-repositories.html]("https://help.ubuntu.com/ubuntu/desktopguide/C/extra-repositories.html")
[https://help.ubuntu.com/ubuntu/desktopguide/C/codecs.html]("https://help.ubuntu.com/ubuntu/desktopguide/C/codecs.html")
(the instructions in the first URL must be followed before those in the second URL)

### Post by bladefallcon on 2006-07-25
ok...I know im probably dreaming asking for this...but does anyone know of a way for Flash (not the player, the development tool) to run on linux, or a suitable substitue?i love this program, speant alot of money to get it...and would love to be able to use it outside of the constraints of windows.

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-07-25
Flash MX runs in WINE, apparantly even with the WINE DLLs. Maybe later versions of Flash do the same thing? See [http://frankscorner.org/index.php?p=flashmx]("http://frankscorner.org/index.php?p=flashmx")

Andthegang, looks like the Linux marketing message isn't getting through. There are *no* viruses for Linux at the moment, so you've no need for anti-virus. If one comes out, try ClamAV (it scans for Windows viruses too). The same goes for spyware - there's none. Same for "unwanted changes" - the various Linux security systems protect against those things.

There is a rootkit detector, but I don't know its name. I don't think it's something you need to worry about unless you're running a server.

In terms of firewall: If you're accessing the Internet through Ubuntu, then the likelihood is that you've got an broadband router of some kind, and therefore are behind a firewall already. Otherwise, try Firestarter.

---

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-07-25
> **Piney said:**
> I get this error when trying to install xchat and xmms

Have you activated the Multiverse and Universe repositories? I know XMMS is in Universe.

---

### Post by Sef on 2006-07-25
> There are *no* viruses for Linux at the moment, so you've no need for anti-virus. If one comes out, try ClamAV (it scans for Windows viruses too).

That is true about viruses for Linux; however, if you run a mail client, then you need to have an anti-virus, so you don't infect your friends.  Your machine can be a virus carrier.

---

### Post by Vertabreaker on 2006-07-25

### Post by Sef on 2006-07-25
> This might be a dumb question, but, the most of the programs in this list that I've looked up don't state anything about being Ubuntu compatible...am I to assume that they'll run without a problem?

If they are from the Ubuntu repositories, they almost always work.

If not, it depends on the program, the software on the computer, and the computer hardware.

### Post by avtolle on 2006-07-26
I don't believe that PDFs can be edited by OO Writer. It can create a PDF. To my knowledge, KWriter (and perhaps Abiword) can edit PDFs. Aysiu has posted on this topic at least a few times, so perhaps a search could clear this up.

### Post by TheWizzard on 2006-07-27
There is a CLI programme called pdftk in the universe repo. pdftk has the following functions: 

Merge PDF documents 
Split PDF pages into a new document 
Decrypt input as necessary (password required) 
Encrypt output as desired 
Fill PDF Forms with FDF Data and/or Flatten Forms 
Apply a Background Watermark 
Report PDF on metrics, including metadata and bookmarks 
Update PDF Metadata 
Attach Files to PDF Pages or the PDF Document 
Unpack PDF Attachments 
Burst a PDF document into single pages 
Uncompress and re-compress page streams 
Repair corrupted PDF (where possible)


hope this helps.

Also it shares an issue with GIMP, which is undoubtedly a fine alternative to Adobe Photoshop. While my tablet can be used to move the cursor, there is NO pressure support. While I'm sure this seems unimportant to many, this is eleminating one of the many advantages that makes a digitizing tablet worth buying. Also, I need to find something that I can animate with. ~$ sudo apt-get install linux-headers-'uname -r'h

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-08-02
I'm no command-line expert, but I don't think you can substitute commands within arguments like that.

You will need to execute "uname -r" first in a terminal, then copy and paste the result into the apt-get command.

### Post by 3rdalbum on 2006-08-05
Can you install that exact package from Synaptic? If not, then you need to enable the Universe and Multiverse repositories.

If it's just apt-get that's giving you grief, then try:

```
sudo apt-get update
```

If that doesn't solve your problem, try:

```
sudo apt-get -f install
```

### Post by calvinthomas on 2006-08-07
Gaim is a good alternative to msn messenger because it is easily available in the repositories and supports almost every IM client i.e MSN, Yahoo, AOL etc. It isn't as 'pretty' as MSN messenger but then again it also isn't such a memory hog and doesn't have any of the annoying adverts.

There are others which are more MSN like I think but i'm afraid I haven't used them as Gaim works perfectly for me

Calv

### Post by calvinthomas on 2006-08-07
I think a similar one to MSN is called aMSN, perhaps give Kopete a try aswell, however I haven't used either, you can change the resolution of your system, I'm now in Kubuntu not Ubuntu so I can't remember exactly but in one of the menus at the top of the screen (the one where you go to update manager I think!) there is a screen resolution (or display resolution) click on that and you can change it!

Calv

### Post by Shampyon on 2006-10-04
You might have to enable the other repositories.

[QUOTE=http://monkeyblog.org/ubuntu/installing/#enabling_extra_repositories]To enable the rest of the Ubuntu repositories you open Synaptic and select an option in its menubar: Settings &#8594; Repositories. Here is a list of the current repositories. To enable the missing section select each of the packages that are labeled binary, click on Edit and tick the boxes outside the sections of the Ubuntu repositories you want to enable.[/QUOTE]

[Animated gif showing how to enable the extra repositories]("http://monkeyblog.org/ubuntu/videos/Extra_repositories.gif") (1237.48 KB)

---

### Post by abu-fatu on 2006-10-04
install alien using synaptic.
download limewirelinux.rpm to desktop
open terminal and type "cd Desktop"
then type "sudo alien -i LimeWireLinux.rpm"
this is how i installed limewire for linux. imho it works much better that frostwire.

### Post by quarkhirad on 2006-12-01
I am sorry i know this is not in the multi/universe section and also its freeware. Infact it has to be downloaded from the net, But i could not help myself after using this software.

Its called yamipod. 
Its use is to sync ur ipod. It can be used insted of gtkpod.

You can download the latest version from [http://www.yamipod.com/main/modules/downloads/](http://www.yamipod.com/main/modules/downloads/)

after that just click on the yamipod for linux (Gtk 2.0).

Its a tarball file. Just extract it and you will get 3 files. One is a libfmodex file , a readme.txt and a executable file called yamipod. Just double click on the executable file and it will start yamipod.

Note:
1)before starting yamipod make sure you copy the libfmodex to ur library folder. 
2)connect ur ipod and make sure its mounted

### Post by Shampyon on 2007-02-03
> **Mouldy1 said:**
> I,m starting a course in early Febuary ,IT Networking(cert 4), and have been told I'll need:

Dreamweaver 8
Photoshop cs2
MS office 2006 ?

I should be able to get around MS office by using Open Office org,But I'm not real sure what to use instead of Dreamweaver and Photoshop( mabye Screem ) ???

Although I'll still need to use the above mentioned software,I don't want to loose touch with my Linux based system as I've found Ubuntu and Kubuntu so much easier to use than that other o/s.

Few people in my area use Linux, I hope by learning a bit about the alternatives I may be able to pass this knowledge on to other future IT and networking profesionals in my class.

I'm also a bit of a noob when it comes to forums so if I'm asking in the wrong place could you direct me elswhere ? :)

Any advice would be great.

NVU is a great HTML editor. It works best if you know a little basic HTML, but the same can be said of Dreamweaver (which produces awfully clogged code if you don't use it just right).

Most people will say GIMP or GIMPShop (a hack of GIMP with more PS-user friendly menus) to replace Photoshop, but you'll find it's a pretty steep learning curve. I use it for basic editing, but I haven't taken the time to learn how to do any of those great fancy things that are so easy in Photoshop. PS is one of the few things I use Windows for. However, you'll find that earlier versions of Photoshop can be made to run well under WINE, so if you're happy not using the latest version try that out.

Almost edit: I just came across this guide to installing Photoshop CS2 on Ubuntu:
[http://blog.publicidadpixelada.com/how-to-adobe-photoshop-cs2-on-ubuntu-10-steps/](http://blog.publicidadpixelada.com/how-to-adobe-photoshop-cs2-on-ubuntu-10-steps/)

I haven't tried it, so I can't tell you if it works, but it's worth a shot!

### Post by vanadium on 2007-04-21
The wiki is an excellent place to start, also for newbies. From [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Home?action=show&redirect=FrontPage](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Home?action=show&redirect=FrontPage)
"Community documentation" brings you to the community documentation. The links under "Start here", "Switching from other OS" and "After you've installed Ubuntu are great in guiding you through your first steps.

One advice, take it slowly first. Do not try to get all what you want the first day. After two weeks, I am all set up and Windows is not anymore an option for me.

I have to confess though that my entire "transition" actually took longer: I already tried Mandrake a couple of years ago, then remained in Windows, albeit solely with the Free Software that I now find back on Ubuntu. Therefore, the transition for me wasn't very dramatic anymore.

### Post by Shampyon on 2007-05-27
To create an ISO you can just rightclick on the disc drive, choose "Copy Disc" and change the burning todeive to "Create image." To burn an ISO, you can just right-click on an ISO and choose "Write To Disc." You could also use Gnomebaker for both.

To mount an ISO, you can use the script in this thread:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=87369&highlight=nautilus+script+mount+iso](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=87369&highlight=nautilus+script+mount+iso)

You have to right-click on the ISO to mount and unmount. It mounts as a virtual hard drive though, not a virtual-cd.

---

### Post by spacejaysis on 2007-07-23
Hi Everyone,
I've been using Feisty for a couple of months and I think I've never had so much fun(!) using a computer. The only thing that keeps me booting back to windows is a program called Locate32. This is a fantastic little app which indexes the name and location of all the files on your PC. You can easily update your index in a matter of minutes and (this is the important bit) when you search for a file by name, size, location or whatever the results are displayed in an explorer-like window. This means you can manipulate the files just the same as if they were in an explorer window: individual or multiple files can be cut, copied, pasted, renamed or whatever.I've tried to find something like this for linux but there only seems to be desktop search engines or content indexers (Beagle, tracker etc.) All I want is to index file names and basic attributes like size, date etc. on demand and be able to manipulate the results in a nautilus or konqueror window, I don't want to index the contents of pdfs, odfs, htmls etc. I've tried 2 progs called Gnome Disk Catalog and GWhere which are more like Locate32 than any other progs, however they only display results, you can even open the files! The author of Locate32 says it was based on GREP and Locate for UNIX so maybe someone knows of a frontend for these programs which would work the way I want. This is really my last stumbling block before I format XP all the way to hell, and I&#7743; looking forward to it. Any help is very much appreciated. Cheers!

### Post by Dipper on 2007-08-20
A more complete list for Kubuntu:

Internet Explorer --------- Konquerer
 
 Microsoft Office --------- OpenOffice.org or KOffice
 ---------------Word --------------- OpenOffice.org Word Processor, KWord
---------------Excel------------------OpenOffice.org Spreadsheet, KSpread
---------------PowerPoint---------OpenOffice.org Presentations, KPresenter
---------------Access---------------Kexi

 Winamp -------- Amarok
 
 Photoshop --------- Krita
 
 AIM, ICQ, MSN, Yahoo!, Jabber, IRC instant messaging --------- Kopete
 
 Word Pad (or notepad) --------- Kate, KWrite
 
 Windows Media Player --------- Kaffeine
 
 iTunes --------- -for playing music:
 -----------------------------Rhythmbox
 ----------------------for iPod Syncing
 --------------------------------Gtkpod
 
 ID3 tag editor ----------------------- easytag
 
 
 MIRC -------- Konversation
 
 Premiere (Movie Editing) --------- kino
 
 Bittorado --------- Bittorado
 (don't you love 
 native ports)
 
 Dreamweaver --------- Kompozer
 
 CDex ---------- KAudioCreator 
 
 Nero -------- K3B
 
 Outlook Express --------- Kontact, Thunderbird
 
 Snood ---------- Frozen-bubble
 
 Partition Magic --------- Qtparted
 
 eMule ----------- aMule
 Soulseek ------------- Nicotine
 DC++ -------------- Valknut
 any multitorrent client ------------ Azureus
 Limewire ------------------ Frostwire
 any download manager --------------- D4X or Gwget
 regedit -------------------- gconf 
 
 Adobe Illustrator ------------ Karbon 14, Xara Xtreme
 
 Remote Desktop Connection ------------ Terminal Server Client

Adobe Acrobat ------------------- KPDF

QuarkXPress, PageMaker -------------- Scribus

---

### Post by rsambuca on 2007-08-20
> **Tamacracker said:**
> I need a program that will let me split an MP3... or at least cut our segments of it. I finally got my Motorola SLVR to connect with my PC vai Bluetooth. My next mission is to modify my favorite mp3s and save them as ringtones for my cellphone. I'd like to cut out segments of my songs in which are my favorite and would love to have as a ring tone.


Anyone know what program I should get? I don't know of any just yet.

I use Audacity for stuff like that.  It is in the repos so you can install it using Synaptic Package Manager, or via the terminal using the command "sudo apt-get install audacity"

You can merger audio files, cut them up, equalize, amplify, etc,.  You can also save them in virtually any format you choose.

### Post by cypress.cynthia on 2007-08-21
> **marym said:**
> Very new to Ubuntu,  I am not even sure I am using the correct language, but here goes.  On my Windows pc/laptop I can choose to send printing to a "ghost" printer which converts the document I am looking at into a pdf.

Where can I find a similar application for use with Feisty Fawn?

You don't have to install a ghost printer in Ubuntu in order to create PDF documents, because OpenOfice already comes with the export to PDF option. Just look for the "Export Directly as PDF" button on the Standard Toolbar, press it, type a name for the new document and that's it. :-D In fact, I used it in Windows in order to create PDF documents from text documents, although I also had installed the  PDF4Free ghost printer which was only used in order to create PDF documents from photos in Adobe Photoshop Album Starter.

---

### Post by cypress.cynthia on 2007-08-21
On second thought, if you do not want to create PDF documents using OpenOffice, you can easily install a PDF Printer in Ubuntu by typing: sudo apt-get install cups-pdf in the terminal. I have just discovered that I must have the cups-pdf package installed in order to use PDFKreator. :(

Later Edit: Actually, PDFKreator doesn't need cups-pdf in order to work. Instead, it needs GhostScript which can be installed by typing sudo apt-get install gs-common in the terminal. I also found[ this guide]("http://ubuntu.wordpress.com/2006/03/23/print-to-pdf-using-cups-pdf/") for configuring CUPS-PDF. You will certainly need it.

Sorry for this off-topic post.

---

### Post by cypress.cynthia on 2007-08-21
> **marym said:**
> I am sorry to be a nuisance.  Here goes.  I have to log into our credit union's bank account every morning to download an spreadsheet (no problem there, it works with Open office).  I then have to "print" the web page.  On my Windows laptop I have something called PrimoPDF which acts as a pretend printer and sends everything to a pdf file.  That is anything that is not an open office file.

Mary

In this, case you really need to download and install CUPS-PDF (CUPS is the Common UNIX Printing System) and CUPS-PDF is the PDF printer of this system. These two guides will show you how to install and configure it: [Print to PDF using cups-pdf]("http://ubuntu.wordpress.com/2006/03/23/print-to-pdf-using-cups-pdf/"), [&#8216;Print&#8217; anything to a PDF Document in GNU/Linux]("http://cuasan.wordpress.com/2007/03/01/print-anything-to-a-pdf-document-in-gnulinux/"). I discovered them by accident today, so I haven't tried either of them yet. Please, let me know which one worked for you.

P:S: Sorry, If I haven't been clear enough in my previous answer.

---

### Post by marym on 2007-08-21

Mary

### Post by BruisedQuasar07 on 2007-10-23
Old Linux users prefer Konqueror over Firefox. Migrating from Windows
to Linux in July at first I did not comprehend why Konqueror. I think I
know why now. Certain site's pages come up near unreadable under
Linux Firefox. I never had this problem under Windows Firefox.

For streaming audio & video from the Net Movie Player with the correct
gstreamer package not only allows it seemlessly, the codec package is
actually superior to Windows Media Player. Often Windows users would
be stopped by "this codec not available", "Cannot find suitable Media 
Player codec" etc. I never get that now under Linux.

I only get stopped by Real Player ...but I haven't installed the Real Player
package for Linux & I will not. Real Player sticks junk on PCs.

--Bruised

### Post by wordchisler on 2008-02-07
1) I'm looking for an **Internet Lock** equivalent to **password protect browsers** (Firefox, Opera). Ideally, Pidgin won't be password protected.

2) is there an equivalent for the startup folder (Windows Start menu)?
 For example, to auto connect to Pidgin after login?

---

### Post by uc50_ic4more on 2008-02-07
> **wordchisler said:**
> 2) is there an equivalent for the startup folder (Windows Start menu)?
 For example, to auto connect to Pidgin after login?

System -> Preferences -> Sessions

You will find yourself, at that point, in the "Startup Programs" tab. Click the "Add" button and insert pidgin as the Command and something appropriate in the Name and Comment fields.

### Post by mahiyar on 2008-04-11
Etusha -- to shutdown your pc automatically type this from your terminal >>sudo shutdown -h +XX.XX &, where XX.XX is the time from now you need to shutdown, instead of +XX.XX you can also give the exact time. The "&" at the end is to run the command in background.

### Post by Shampyon on 2008-04-26
> **quarkhirad said:**

Hi. I'm new to Ubuntu and a program I used to use loads on windows was a referencing/citation program called EndNote. ([http://www.endnote.com/](http://www.endnote.com/)) It basically creates a library of textbooks/journals/websites/papers etc and adds a toolbar to word. You can then click once on the toolbar to generate a citation in a word document. Really useful program if you a student or postgrad and write a lot of reports. Does anyone know of any program like this for OpenOffice?

### Post by sybille on 2008-07-17
> **Matthew7630 said:**
> Hi. I'm new to Ubuntu and a program I used to use loads on windows was a referencing/citation program called EndNote. ([http://www.endnote.com/](http://www.endnote.com/)) It basically creates a library of textbooks/journals/websites/papers etc and adds a toolbar to word. You can then click once on the toolbar to generate a citation in a word document. Really useful program if you a student or postgrad and write a lot of reports. Does anyone know of any program like this for OpenOffice?

Hi, Matthew7630.

You could try Zotero:
[http://www.zotero.org/](http://www.zotero.org/)

Here are some tips for using Zotero on Ubuntu:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Zotero](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Zotero)
There are instructions there for installing the extension that makes Zotero work with OpenOffice.org Writer.

Also, at the bottom of that wiki page, there are links to some alternatives to Zotero:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Zotero#Alternatives%20to%20Zotero](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Zotero#Alternatives%20to%20Zotero)
